text:
A hit! I used country bone in pork ribs. I made the sauce according to direction but I didn't have any steak sauce and used a splash of soy sauce and put a bit more garlic in. The 3 men in my house went ga-ga over this. I thought it might taste a smidgen too ketchupy but the guys  absolutely loved it and said I was crazy - lol. This did make a gooey sauce that stuck to the ribs and didn't run off. The meat literally fell away from the bone. We will make this again and again. Thank you for a new family favorite.

text:
I made this with country style boneless ribs. I put them in the crockpot ontop of a layer of vidiala onions. When they were done I transfered them to a baking pan and spread "The Sauce" on both the bottom and tops and baked at 350 for 1/2 hour. Wonderful! I had cut "The Sauce" recipe in 1/2 and still had a ton left. A few days later I made a oven roasted brisket from Paula Deen and served the remaining sauce with it. Dh now will eat it no other way! Will definatly use "The Sauce" when ever we BBQ! Thanks for posting!

text:
These are by far the very best ribs I have ever made.  The meat falls right off the bone.  And the sauce is to die for.  I plan on using this sauce for different meats also.  I had someof the sauce left over so I brushed it on Chicken breasts.  They were just as good as the ribs.  It is the sauce that is the real killer in this recipe.  I like to just make batches of the sauce and keep it in the fridge for just about any type of meat.  Give it a try.

text:
I disagree with the reviewer who said that bottled sauce would be better. This sauce was super! I added finely chopped onion and bottled chili sauce and soy sauce to taste. It was excellent! I always parboil ribs before grilling, but I've never finished them off in the oven as this recipe directs.  The texture and flavor of the meat really reminded me of carolina pulled pork. YUMMY!!!  One suggestion -- Add a quatered onion, some crushed fresh garlic, peppercorns and salt to the cooking water. It really adds depth of flavor to the meat itself. I've also added beer and/or apple cider vinegar to the cooking water in past. Mmmm!!

This is a keeper recipe! I ran short of ketchup and made it up with BBQ sauce, but it came out fine. We used Sonny's Mild BBQ sauce for a sweet sauce, but the pork came out like Carolina BBQ - tender enough to eat with a fork. We substituted 5 lbs country style pork ribs for the 2 lbs spareribs and still had a smidgen of sauce left (which I will save). Thank you for a wonderful way to cook ribs inside the house. My husband and mother both want me to make this again - frequently.

text:
These are awesome!  I never vary from the original recipe the first time I make something - and I'm glad I didn't with these.  The second time I made them, I didn't quite have all the ingredients so these are the changes I made - 1) used less ketchup - only 1 1/2 cups. 2) Didnt have any worcestershire, so I used 1/3 cup of liquid smoke. 3) I used the rest of the ingredients as stated.  The only other thing I did different was I added the garlic to the meat while it was boiling and also threw in a sliced onion.  Either way you make these, you absolutely CAN'T go wrong.  Thank you for a wonderful recipe!

text:
Love it! I was sceptical at first like some about boiling the ribs and losing flavor of the meat (boiled meat ew) but it was fine. The only change I made was I added some lawrys seasoning to the water (thought what could it hurt). Now as for this sauce everyone is so gung ho about, I was not really feeling it while it was simmering on the stove. I followed the recipe pretty close. Used only 2 cups of ketchup after reading the other reviews because I hate a ketchupy sauce. Cut back on the sugar a little because I used KC masterpiece Honey for the bbq sauce and I didn't want it to be too sweet. I added a little sauteed onions and soy sauce also. It was really thick so I thinned it out with a little of the cooking liquid from the ribs. There was a ton of sauce since I only used 2.5 lbs of spareribs but I love my ribs smothered in sauce and these definitely were. They were awesome. Tender and flavorful. Sauce turned out perfect after baking the ribs in it. This ones a keeper for me. Thanks!

text:
Great recipe except I never, ever, ever, never, never boil ribs - hence the 4 out of 5 stars. I just added the ingredients to the ribs and put them in the oven. You end up losing SO much flavor and the meat isn't as juicy because most of the fat ends up in the water. You need the fat for self basting and that also enhances flavor! You just end up "masking" the taste and juiciness with the sauce.

Wow!  These are so good. I admit, I was a bit skeptical about the sauce as it sounded like someone opened their refrigerator door and started dumping stuff in the pan, but it is AMAZING! This is the first review I have ever written on this site. I have used dozens of recipes from here but tend to take bits and pieces from a few similar ones and blend them together to make my own dish. I decided that Sunday was the day that I would actually follow a recipe to the "T". I had spare ribs in the fridge and decided on your recipe as it held a trustworthy 5 star rating. AHA!! I found the secret. The reason some people have had trouble with this recipe. Last week Hubby bought baby back ribs. But not enough to suit me, and not enough to have leftovers! When he picked up more on his way home yesterday, he had gotten pork spareribs. Like from adult porkers. I mixed all the ribs together to boil, then bake. Not surprisingly, the BABY backs were perfect. The big ones were horrible. I took a bite, chewed, chewed, and ended up spitting it out. Today I took all the big ribs, put them in a baking dish with water, covered, then steamed on low heat for 2 1/2 hours.
PERFECTION! Added a little more sauce to perk them up after cooking, left covered. So happy.

text:
I have finally found my rib recipe! Followed recipe exactly, except for I threw in a few garlic cloves and a splash of liquid smoke into the water that I boiled the ribs in.  I used baby back ribs and a honey garlic BBQ sauce.  I love how the sauce actually sticks to the ribs.  They were nice and tender and I didn't have to slow cook them all day.  A definite keeper, thank you so much Sylvia!  Update:  I've learned that if you're using a sweet BBQ sauce, it's best to either cut down the sugar by half or eliminate completely.  I've used this on chicken too - both in the slow cooker (shredded after cooking for a BBQ chicken sandwich) and on the grill.

text:
These ribs were decent.  I used it on pork ribs, which are fattier yet more flavorful than beef ribs.  Boiling them for so long seemed to remove most of the flavor, and didn't seem to get rid of much of the fat.  The meat ended up very tender, and tasting mostly of the sauce.  I prefer to use a rub on my ribs, bake them for 1-2 hours in a slow oven, then cover them with a barbecue sauce and grill or broil them for a few minutes.  They're still tender, and they haven't had all their natural flavor  boiled away.

text:
I boiled my ribs for about 20 minutes, threw them in the crock pot on low with about half the BBQ sauce for about 5 hours.  Then I took them out and put them on a baking sheet, brushed them with the remaining BBQ sauce and baked about 15 minutes then I flipped them and brushed the other side and baked 15 more minutes.  These were the PERFECT ribs and it was the BBQ sauce that made them that way!  My husband (who rarely compliments a meal) couldn't stop raving about these ribs.  He even called his mother!  Thanks Sylvia for the recipe!  I'll be using this forever.

text:
The ribs turned out great!...very tender and falling off the bone.  I've been wanting to find an oven based recipe for ribs for those times when we don't feel like grilling out or when it is inconvenient to do so.  I tried a few other recipes in the past.  The results were alright but not good enough to do again.  This one is a keeper.  The submitter of this recipe makes a good point about adjusting the ingredients to suite your tastes.  In our case, we used honey BBQ sauce because that's what we had on hand.  That combined with the brown sugar made the sauce much sweeter than we would have preferred.  Next time, we'll use a tangier BBQ sauce and reduce the amount of brown sugar.  The most important parts of this recipe are the actual cooking instructions.  The ingredients can be and should be experimented with and altered as you see fit so that you end up with the type of flavor you and your family prefer.

Everyone LOVED them.  This is my "go to" rib recipe for now on. text:
My family loved it. I modified the recipe a little (hence why I deducted a star) to make pulled pork sandwiches.
I mixed 1 cup ketchup, 1.5 cups BBQ sauce (used a local brand Texas Texas BBQ and grilling sauce). I didn't add any sugar as I usually find this too sweet, used about 1.5 tablespoons lemon juice, 1 tablespoon chili garlic sauce, 2 tablespoons of minced garlic. I didn't have steak sauce but used 1 tablespoon of cider vinegar. I mixed all of these ingredients to make the sauce.   I boiled the ribs and then placed them in a slow cooker with diced onions at the bottom and alternating layers of ribs and sauce. I cooked it on low for 7 hours. Turned out great. Could use mor chili sauce for those that like a little kick.  Now I am just looking for a BBQ sauce recipe that I can make at home rather than buying from the store (although this sauce was fantastic)

These are the BEST of the BEST!  I have never been quite satisfied with ribs until now...I boiled 3 pounds of boneless country-style  pork ribs with 2 Tbsp garlic salt, 1 Tbsp Lawry's seasoning, and 1 tsp ground pepper for 1 and 1/2 hours at a low simmer.  Then I baked them in about 1/3 the sauce for another hour or so and left them covered the entire time.  Tender, flavored perfectly, delicious!

WOW DELICIOUS!  I added 3/4 cup of honey, and only about half of the ketchup.  I also added 3 bay leaves, sliced onion, and chopped garlic, to my rib water while boiling.  I actually lost 2 of the bones off the ends trying to get them out of the pot, they were so tender!  I was going to serve these with baked sweet potatos, but my kids like brown sugar on those, and there is plenty of sweetness in the rib sauce, so went with baked potato, with sour cream, and steamed broccoli with cheese sauce. In my opinion, this turned out like resaurant quality ribs.  Truely delicious!  THANK YOU SYLVIA, for giving me a place to start or my own sauce.  As a fan of "sweet baby rays" sauce for a LONG time, I have to say...sorry ray..I can handle that sauce myself now. ;)

I need to update my review of this recipe.  I made this a couple years ago and absolutely loved it.  When I boil my ribs I add spices and an onion in the water to add flavor in the meat.  Mainly fresh garlic, onion powder, salt and pepper, maybe a little liquid smoke.  Season the water really well.  Or most of the time what I use in place of the water is dr pepper.  It really helps tenderize your meat.  The one thing about this recipe, that makes it 5 stars is the sauce! I tell you what, this sauce is Phenomenal!  Very tangy and delicious!  It makes a big batch of sauce.  Almost double what I need for our ribs.  Which is great, because I save the extra for next time!  Great recipe Sylvia!

text:
I just made this tonight for supper, and I'm glad I did.  These were just great.  My husband who isn't a real big ribs fan loved these. I did change the recipe just a bit though.  I decreased the amount of ketchup by about 3/4 of a cup because I was afraid the sauce would end up tasting to much like just ketchup, and I increase the garlic to 4 cloves because we love garlic.  The meat was extremely tender and juicy.  I will be making these again, even my husband asked  me to make them again while we were still having dinner. I do agree with one of the othere reviewers who said that the recipe could be halfed and still there would be enough sauce.  Thanks Sylvia  Update 2009 I am constantly making these ribs with different variations.  I have found that we like them best if we finish them on the bbq letting the sauce caramelize instead of finishing them in the oven uncovered (when we do it this way we leave the ribs intack and slice them after taking them off the bbq)

These spareribs are absolutely delicious!
I have been using a recipe very similar to this one for years, although this one leaves more room for the imagination.  It's so good and the combination of boiling the ribs and then baking them in the oven ensures tender, fall of the bone ribs every time. text:
Thanks to Sylvia, I finally I made perfect pork spare ribs. I've always been told I'm a fantastic cook but trying to make really moist, fall off the bone tender spare ribs has made me feel otherwise.  I haven't tried to make them too often in my 72 years but my husbands really enjoys good pork ribs so I've tried from time to time with different recipes. I've come up with great flavor but  the ribs were always less than perfectly melt in your mouth tender. Not this time. THIS RECIPE IS FANTASTIC!!! 

Since she made a note about soy sauce and onions I added a large chopped onion and 3 cloves of chopped garlic to the water the ribs boiled in for an extra layer of flavor.  I also added 1/2 cup of soy sauce to the sauce.  I had everything on hand but steak sauce. They were out of this world anyway.  I'm positive exactly as written this is one of the best rib recipe around so do that first. Then, as Sylvia says, play around with ingredients to suit your taste. 

This will be my only go to recipe to use again but I'm also going to try making my favorite ribs... Chinese Spare Ribs. I'll use her method but  will substitute ingredients for Chinese ribs.

Last time I was at my butcher shop,  I noticed an unusual item in the meat case. Veal ribs ! I bought some and was planning to use the same bbq rib recipe from AR, I've been using for years, "barbecued beef ribs for 2". But,  I noticed  the good rating of this recipe and decided to give it a try. I am glad I did.
I kept the sauce the same. but went ahead and flavored the boiling water with 1 quartered onion, 2 crushed garlic  cloves , 2 bay leaves, some pepper corns and 2 teaspoon salt.
The ribs were tender and  finger licking good. And FYI, You will have at least 1/3 of the sauce leftover.

text:
Great recipe! My family loves these ribs. I have made them several times and only made a couple small changes.
For one rack of ribs, I cut the recipe in half, but still use 2 cloves of garlic. I only use about 1 cup of ketchup and make up for that by adding more BBQ sauce. It's more tangy and less ketchupy tasting. I didn't have hot pepper sauce on hand, so I added some Sweet and Spicy BBQ sauce (safeway brand). The ribs always turn out amazing!

text:
OMG these were Fabulous!!  I don't usually posts reviews, but this recipe just too good not too.
I think that it is great as is, but here were my spins....didn't have enough ketchup, so I used half chili sauce & half ketchup....it was a good swap out! I boiled the ribs in salted water with half a can of beer and 2 crushed garlic cloves added to the water. Used crushed red in the sauce...didn't have tabasco worked fine....the sauce is the best one out there....my guys are still gushing...used a half recipe and it was plenty for 2 racks (6 lbs total) of St. Louis cut ribs. Make sure to cut them up before putting in the oven, like the recipe says....better sauce coverage and it thickens better.  A Keeper,,,,THANKS!!!!!!!

I will never use another sauce ever again. Thanks for the recipe!

text:
I had my doubts; I've boiled up ribs before and grilled them and they're tough, but basically went with this recipe because I had all the ingredients.  I did halve the sauce, and it was plenty for ribs (for family of 2 adults/2young kids).  I think I reduced par-boil time to 40 minutes, and since I didn't have steak sauce, I subbed 1/8 tsp of liquid smoke, and a couple tbl of red-wine vinegar.  I also eliminated the hot sauce since my kids haven't acquired the taste for heat.  These were just fabulous....tender, awesome bbq sauce - thick, sweet, and stick-to-your-fingers!  Ribs were tender and easily came off the bone.  HUGE thumbs up!!!!

Taste-wise, my family rated this tops, thus the 5 stars. Issues with this recipe are in terms of proportions. First, 2 pounds of ribs barely fed 3 people and these are not big eaters. Second, half the sauce more than adequately covered this amount of ribs, so if you don't want a lot of leftover barbecue sauce don't make the entire batch. Make sure to line your roasting pan with foil. The dishwasher will thank you. Thanks for the recipe.
